Existence as Attribute or Essence? The Role of Aḥwāl
Al-Sāwī explains the conditional validity of existence as an essential attribute and its status as a mental consideration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the status of existence as an attribute depends on one's position on the doctrine of aḥwāl, and how existence is understood as a mental consideration when it is identical to the essence.

Core Idea
Existence as attribute stays or falls with the doctrine of states.

This passage from al-Sāwī's commentary tackles a subtle theological dispute: is existence itself a distinct attribute of God, or is it just another way of saying He exists? The answer hinges on whether one affirms the 'states' (aḥwāl) as intermediate realities. Al-Sāwī clarifies the positions and then offers a vivid analogy to explain how existence can be merely a mental consideration.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the literal translation. Note the structure: first a conditional statement, then an explanation of the opposite view, then an analogy.
Pay attention to the key terms: وجود, صفة نفسية, أحوال, أمر اعتباري.
2
Identify the two positions on aḥwāl
The passage distinguishes between those who affirm aḥwāl and those who deny them. How does each view affect whether existence is an attribute? Understand the reasoning behind each.
3
Analyze the analogy of the garment
Al-Sāwī compares existence to the 'appearance' of a garment. Why is appearance a mental consideration? How does this analogy help clarify that existence is not an external entity?
This step connects the abstract doctrine to a concrete example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجَعْلُ الوجود صفةً نفسيَّة إِنَّما يصح عند من يُثبت الأحوال، فيكون صفة زائدة على الذات، غير موجودة في نفسها، ولا معدومة، وأما عند من لم يُثبت الأحوال فليس بصفة أصلاً، وإنما هو عين ذات الموجود كما مرّ . قوله: (وإنَّما هو عين ذات الموجود) : أي : فليس أمراً ثابتاً في الخارج؛ كالقدرة والإرادة، فلا ينافي أنَّه أمر اعتباري يعتبره الشَّخص ذهناً فقط، وذلك كما إذا أخرجت ثوباً من صندوق مثلاً، فالثّوب يوصف بالظهور، وهو أمر اعتباري لا ثبوت له في الخارج بحيث يصح أن يرى ولا في نفسه، بل هو أمر يعتبره الشَّخص في نفسه فقط .
And making existence an essential attribute is only valid according to one who affirms the states (al-aḥwāl), so it would be an attribute additional to the essence, not existing in itself nor non-existent. But according to one who does not affirm the states, it is not an attribute at all; rather it is the very essence of the existent, as has passed. His saying: (Rather it is the very essence of the existent) meaning: so it is not a thing established externally, like power and will, so it does not contradict that it is a mental consideration (amr iʿtibārī) that a person considers only mentally. That is like when you take out a garment from a chest, for example, the garment is described as 'appearing', which is a mental consideration having no external establishment such that it could be seen, nor in itself, but it is a thing that a person considers only in his mind.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of the attribute of existence (al-wujūd) when made an essential attribute (ṣifa nafsiyya). The commentator states that making existence an essential attribute is only valid according to those who affirm the 'states' (aḥwāl). According to them, existence would be an attribute additional to the essence, not existing in itself nor non-existent in the way that meanings exist. However, according to those who do not affirm states (i.e., the majority of Ashʿarīs who deny aḥwāl), existence is not an attribute at all; rather, it is identical to the essence (ʿayn dhāt al-mawjūd). The commentator then explains that 'being the very essence of the existent' means it is not an external entity like power and will. This does not contradict the fact that it is a mental consideration (amr iʿtibārī) that a person considers only in the mind. The commentator gives an analogy: when you take a garment out of a chest, the garment is described as 'appearing', which is a mental consideration with no external existence such that it could be seen or exist in itself. It is simply something the person considers in his mind.

Key Terms
الوجود
الصفة النفسية
الأحوال
أمر اعتباري
عين الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Existence is always a distinct attribute of God, separate from His essence.
Correction: The commentator explains that existence is only considered a distinct attribute by those who affirm aḥwāl; for others, it is identical to the essence and not an attribute at all.

Checkpoint
According to those who deny aḥwāl, how is the attribute of existence described?
A) An additional attribute existing externally
B) An attribute non-existent in itself
C) The very essence of the existent
D) A state caused by power

Key Takeaway
Whether existence is considered a distinct attribute or identical to the essence depends on one's acceptance of the doctrine of aḥwāl; when taken as identical, existence is a mental consideration, not an external reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you tend to think of God's existence as something added to His essence, like an extra quality? How does this passage challenge you to reconsider the simplicity of God? Commit today to study the concept of tawheed more deeply, so you never conceive of God's attributes as separate from His essence in a way that compromises His oneness.
?
The text says existence can be a 'mental consideration' – something we grasp intellectually but not as a separate reality. How does this affect your understanding of God's self-sufficiency? Are you content with knowing God through His names and attributes, or do you secretly wish for a tangible proof? The Objection on Existence and the Ashʿarī Negation of States
Objection that following Ashʿarī's negation of states should exclude existence, and the reply distinguishing states from considerations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the commentator includes existence as an attribute despite following al-Ashʿarī's negation of states, and how the distinction between states (aḥwāl) and mental considerations (iʿtibārāt) resolves the objection.

Core Idea
Negating states does not negate mental considerations; existence is a mental addition needed for building attributes.

This lesson addresses a key objection: if the creed is built on al-Ashʿarī's school that negates states (aḥwāl), why include existence as an attribute? The commentator replies by distinguishing between states and mental considerations (iʿtibārāt), showing that existence is a necessary mental addition. This distinction is central to understanding how kalam handles divine attributes without falling into multiplicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice the objector's challenge and the commentator's two-part response.
The response first appeals to necessity, then to a higher verification.
2
Identify the distinction between aḥwāl and iʿtibārāt
The commentator argues that al-Ashʿarī negates states but not mental considerations. Understand what makes iʿtibārāt acceptable even without external existence.
This is the core of the reply.
3
Reflect on why existence is foundational
The commentator says existence is needed to build other attributes. Consider why affirming existence is necessary before any other attribute can be discussed.
This connects to the structure of kalam arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : إذا كنتَ قد بنيت هذه العقيدة على مذهب الأشعري القائل بنفي الأحوال، فالوجه حذف الوجود، ولا حاجة إلى ارتكاب التسامح. قلتُ : لمَّا كان معرفة الوجود يحتاج لها، لينبني عليها غيرها من الصفات اعتبرت الوصف الظاهري في قولنا : (ذات الله موجودة)، وارتكبت التّسمح ، على أنَّ التَّحقيق أنَّ الشَّيخ ولو نفى الأحوال لا ينفي الاعتبارات لظهور زيادتها ذهناً، وإن لم يكن لها ثبوت خارجاً، بل قال العلامة التفتازاني : لا خلاف أنَّ الوجود زائد ذهناً، أنّ للعقل أن يلاحظ الماهية بدون الوجود، بمعنى قوله : (لينبني عليها غيرها :أي فهي أصل لغيرها، إذ لا يصحُ اتّصافه بصفة إلا بعد إثبات وجوده. قوله : ( على أنَّ التَّحقيق . . . إلخ): ارتقاء في الجواب .
If you say: Since you have built this creed on the school of al-Ashʿarī who holds the negation of states (aḥwāl), then the proper course would be to delete existence, and there is no need to commit tolerance. I say: Because knowledge of existence is needed, so that other attributes may be built upon it, I considered the apparent description in our saying 'The essence of God is existent', and I committed tolerance. But the verification is that the Shaykh, even if he negates states, does not negate considerations (iʿtibārāt) because their mental addition is evident, even if they have no external establishment. Rather, al-Taftāzānī said: There is no disagreement that existence is mentally additional, and that the intellect can observe the quiddity without existence. Meaning his saying: (So that others may be built upon it) i.e., it is a foundation for others, for it is not valid to describe Him with any attribute except after establishing His existence. His saying: (But the verification ... etc.) is an ascent in the answer.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage contains an objection and its answer. The objector says: Since you have built this creed on the Ashʿarī school which negates states (aḥwāl), you should simply delete existence as an attribute; there is no need for tolerance (tasāmuḥ). The commentator replies: Knowledge of existence is needed because other attributes are built upon it; so I considered the apparent description in saying 'The essence of God is existent' and committed tolerance. The verification (taḥqīq) is that the Shaykh (al-Ashʿarī), even though he negates states, does not negate considerations (iʿtibārāt), because their mental addition is evident even if they have no external establishment. The commentator supports this with the statement of al-Taftāzānī: There is no disagreement that existence is mentally additional (zāʾid dhihnan). The intellect can observe the quiddity (māhiyya) without existence. Then the commentator explains the meaning of the phrase 'so that others may be built upon it' (لينبني عليها غيرها): existence is a foundation for other attributes, because it is not valid to describe Him with any attribute except after establishing His existence. The commentator notes that the author's phrase 'on that the verification' (على أنَّ التَّحقيق) is an ascent in the answer, meaning it is a higher level of response.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Negating aḥwāl means negating all mental distinctions about attributes.
Correction: Al-Ashʿarī only negates states (aḥwāl) that would be real mental entities, but he allows mental considerations (iʿtibārāt) which have only conceptual addition.

Key Takeaway
The commentator defends the inclusion of existence as an attribute by arguing that it is a mental consideration (iʿtibār), not a state (ḥāl), and that existence is necessary as a foundation for other attributes.

The Mental Addition of Existence in Divine Attributes
Objection and answer on existence as a mental attribute despite Ash'ari denial of states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'ari theologians affirm existence as a mentally additional attribute despite denying external states, and how this preserves theological coherence.

Core Idea
Existence is mentally added to essence, not an external state, keeping Ash'ari theology consistent.

This lesson addresses a key objection in Ash'ari kalam: if the school denies states (ahwal), how can we speak of existence as an attribute? The author defends the formulation by showing that existence is a mental consideration, not an external state, and it is necessary for building other attributes. The discussion also clarifies the number of 'subsistences' for different categories of attributes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection that existence should be omitted given the Ash'ari denial of states. Note the tension: if there are no real 'states', why treat existence as a separate attribute?
2
Grasp the author's defense
The author justifies retaining existence as a 'mental basis' for other attributes. Even if not an external state, it is a necessary conceptual foundation.
The phrase 'tolerance' (tasāmuh) indicates a concession in wording, not doctrine.
3
Explore mental addition
Taftazani is cited to affirm that existence is mentally additional to essence. The intellect can conceive quiddity without existence, proving its mental distinctness.
This is key: no external state is required for mental addition.
4
Distinguish subsistences
Learn the threefold or fourfold classification: existents have four subsistences (minds, words, souls, external), meanings have three (all but external), and negative attributes have two (words and souls).
This shows how different categories of attributes relate to reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : إذا كنتَ قد بنيت هذه العقيدة على مذهب الأشعري القائل بنفي الأحوال، فالوجه حذف الوجود، ولا حاجة إلى ارتكاب التسامح. قلتُ : لمَّا كان معرفة الوجود يحتاج لها، لينبني عليها غيرها من الصفات اعتبرت الوصف الظاهري في قولنا : (ذات الله موجودة)، وارتكبت التّسمح ، على أنَّ التَّحقيق أنَّ الشَّيخ ولو نفى الأحوال لا ينفي الاعتبارات لظهور زيادتها ذهناً، وإن لم يكن لها ثبوت خارجاً، بل قال العلامة التفتازاني : لا خلاف أنَّ الوجود زائد ذهناً، أنّ للعقل أن يلاحظ الماهية بدون الوجود، بمعنى قوله : (لينبني عليها غيرها :أي فهي أصل لغيرها، إذ لا يصحُ اتّصافه بصفة إلا بعد إثبات وجوده. قوله : ( على أنَّ التَّحقيق . . . إلخ): ارتقاء في الجواب . قوله : ( وإن لم يكن لها ثبوت خارجاً أي فيكون لها ثلاث ثبوتات فقط : ثبوت في الأذهان، وثبوت في الألفاظ، وثبوت في النفوس، بخلاف المعاني وكل موجود؛ فله أربع ثبوتات بزيادة الثبوت في الأعيان، وأما السَّليَّة : فلها ثبوتان ؛ ثبوت في الألفاظ، وثبوت في النفوس. قوله: (أي: يلاحظ الماهيَّة بدون الوجود أي كملاحظة ماهية القول في الذهن مع عدم وجوده في الخارج. قوله : (ثم تليها في الذِّكر): أي لا في الواقع ونفس الأمر، إذ لا ترتيب بين صفات الله تعالى في نفس الأمر، إذ الترتيب يقتضي حدوث وبالعكس، ونتعقَّلُ الماهية ونشكُ فى وجودها) انتهى
If you say: Since you built this creed on the Ash'ari school which negates states, the proper course would be to omit existence, and there is no need to resort to tolerance. I say: Because knowledge of existence is needed, so that other attributes may be built upon it, I considered the apparent description in our statement: 'The essence of God is existent', and I resorted to tolerance, although the truth is that the Shaykh, even if he negates states, does not negate considerations due to the apparentness of their mental addition, even if they have no external subsistence. Rather, al-'Allama al-Taftazani said: There is no disagreement that existence is mentally additional, for the intellect can observe quiddity without existence, meaning his statement: 'so that other attributes may be built upon it' i.e., it is a basis for others, since it is not valid to describe Him with any attribute except after establishing His existence. His statement: 'although the truth... etc.' is an elevation in the answer. His statement: 'even if they have no external subsistence' i.e., they have only three subsistences: subsistence in minds, subsistence in words, and subsistence in souls, unlike meanings and every existent; for it has four subsistences with the addition of subsistence in external entities. As for the negative attributes, they have two subsistences: subsistence in words and subsistence in souls. His statement: 'i.e., he observes quiddity without existence' i.e., like observing the quiddity of a statement in the mind while it has no existence externally. His statement: 'then they follow in mention' i.e., not in reality and actual fact, for there is no order among God's attributes in actual fact, since order necessitates temporality and vice versa, and we conceive quiddity and doubt its existence) ended.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer regarding the inclusion of existence among divine attributes. The objector notes that on Ash'ari doctrine, which denies 'states' (ahwal), existence should not be mentioned as a separate attribute, so the author's phrasing is problematic. The answer explains that existence is treated as a mental consideration (i'tibar) rather than an external state. The author cites Taftazani to affirm that existence is mentally additional to essence, meaning the intellect can conceive of quiddity without existence. The commentary then clarifies that the order of attributes in mention does not imply a real order in God's essence, as that would entail temporality. Finally, it distinguishes the number of 'subsistences' (thubutat) for different categories: existents have four (in minds, words, souls, and external entities), meanings have three (all but external), and negative attributes have two (in words and souls). This shows careful theological nuance in preserving Ash'ari commitments while justifying the doctrinal formulation.

Correction: They deny external states but affirm mental addition; existence is considered a mental consideration (i'tibar) distinct from essence in the mind.

The Five Negative Attributes and Their Scope
Definition of negative attributes and explanation that they are not limited to five.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what negative attributes are, why they are five in number, and why they are called negative, as well as the correct understanding of their scope.

Core Idea
The five negative attributes are the principal negations, but they are not exhaustive.

In this passage, the commentator defines negative attributes (al-sifat al-sualablyya) as those that negate anything unbefitting Allah. He explains why they are called 'negative', why they precede attributes of meaning, and stresses that the five listed are the 'mothers' of all negative attributes, though many more exist. The passage also clarifies a subtle point about the attribute of pre-eternality (qidam).

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of negative attributes
Read the opening where the author states that the five negative attributes are relative to negation (salb), meaning denial (nafy), and each negates something unbefitting Allah.
Note the synonymity of salb, nafy, and adam.
2
Understand the priority of negative over positive attributes
The author compares negative attributes to clearing (takhliya) which precedes adorning (tahliya). This shows that negation of imperfections comes before affirming perfections.
This is a key reason why negative attributes are mentioned first.
3
Recognize that the five are not exhaustive
The author explicitly says 'the truth is that the negative attributes are not limited to these five' and gives examples like no child, no spouse, not being composite, not in place/time/direction.
The five are called 'mothers' because they encompass the main categories.
4
Clarify the intended meaning of qidam
The author notes that qidam (pre-eternality) is not meant to imply another pre-eternality besides Allah, correcting a possible misunderstanding.
This ensures that Allah's attribute of qidam is not seen as contingent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانياً: الصفات السلبية ثم تليها في الذكر خمسة سلبيَّة نسبة للسَّلْب؛ أي : النَّفي، إذ مدلول كل واحد منها سلب أمرٍ لا يليق به سبحانه وهي أي : الصّفات السَّلبيَّة . المرتّب على ما قبله والحدوث عليه وعلى صفاته محال. قوله : (أي: النَّفي) : المراد به العدم، إذ السلب والنَّفي والعدم بمعنى واحد، وقدَّم السَّلبيَّة على المعاني ؛ لأنَّ السَّلبيَّة؛ كالتَّخلية بالخاء المعجمة والمعاني؛ كالتَّحلية بالحاء المهملة، والتخلية مقدمة على التحلية . والحقُّ : أنَّ الصِّفات السَّلبيَّة لا تنحصر في هذه الخمسة، إذ من جملتها أنَّه لا ولد له ولا زوجة ولا بسيطاً ولا مركباً، ولا في مكان ولا زمان ولا جهة، وغير ذلك، وإنَّما اقتصر على هذه الخمسة؛ لأنَّها أمها لها ولا والد لها، وهكذا يقال في باقي الصفات. قوله : (إذ مدلول كل واحدة ... إلخ ) : علَّة لقوله : (نسبة للسَّلبيَّة). قوله : (وليس المراد بالقدم الذاتي ما قابل القدم بالغير) : لأنَّه يوهم أنَّ هناك قدماً بالغير في نفس الأمر، لكن ليس مراداً وليس كذلك .
Secondly: The negative attributes. Then they follow in mention: five negative [attributes], relative to negation (salb); i.e., denial (nafy), since the meaning of each one is the negation of something unbefitting Him, may He be exalted. And they are, i.e., the negative attributes. Arranged upon what precedes, and temporality upon Him and His attributes is impossible. His statement: 'i.e., denial': what is intended is non-existence (adam), for negation (salb), denial (nafy), and non-existence (adam) are synonymous. And he gave priority to negative attributes over the attributes of meaning (ma'ani) because the negative are like clearing (takhliya) with the letter kha', and the attributes of meaning are like adorning (tahliya) with the letter ha', and clearing precedes adorning. The truth is that the negative attributes are not limited to these five; for among them are that He has no child, no spouse, nor is He simple or compound, nor in a place, nor time, nor direction, and so on. He only limited himself to these five because they are the mothers of them, having no father, and similarly is said for the remaining attributes. His statement: 'since the meaning of each one... etc.' is a cause for his statement 'relative to the negative'. His statement: 'And the intended meaning of pre-eternality (qidam) is not that which is contrasted with pre-eternality by another' because it implies that there is a pre-eternality by another in actual fact, but that is not intended, and it is not so.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage defines and discusses the negative attributes (al-sifat al-sualablyya). It explains that they are called negative because each negates something unbefitting God. The author notes that the terms 'salb', 'nafy', and 'adam' are synonymous, all meaning negation or non-existence. He explains why negative attributes are mentioned before the attributes of meaning: they are like clearing (takhliya), which precedes adorning (tahliya). Crucially, the author asserts that the negative attributes are not confined to the five mentioned; many more exist, such as that God has no child, spouse, is not composed, not in space or time. The five are emphasized because they are 'mothers' (principal). The passage also clarifies that the attribute of pre-eternality (qidam) is not meant to imply another pre-eternality besides God. The commentary follows the source's order: definition, priority, scope, and clarification of the intended meaning of qidam.

The Attribute of Pre-eternality (al-Qidam)
Defines al-qidam, distinguishes qadim bil-dhat from qadim bil-ghayr, and discusses azali vs. qadim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-qidam as the negation of beginning, the distinction between essential pre-eternality and pre-eternality through another, and the nuanced relationship between the terms 'qadim' and 'azali'.

Core Idea
Pre-eternality means no beginning; it belongs to Allah by essence, not through another.

This lesson dives into the attribute of al-qidam (pre-eternality). The source passage defines it clearly as the negation of beginning and distinguishes Allah's essential pre-eternality from the philosophical notion of pre-eternality through another. It also clarifies the scope of the term 'everything other than God' and explores the relationship between 'qadim' and 'azali'.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow. Notice that the author starts by affirming essential pre-eternality and then explains its meaning.
The passage contains a rebuttal of a philosophical position and a discussion of terminology.
2
Identify Key Definitions
Locate the definition of al-qidam as 'negation of beginning' (salb al-awwaliyya) and the distinction between qadim bil-dhat and qadim bil-ghayr. Understand that Allah's pre-eternality is not acquired from an external cause.
The author explicitly rejects the possibility of anything being eternal through another.
3
Clarify the Scope of 'Everything Other than God'
Notice the clarification that 'everything other than God' refers only to existents, not to eternal non-existences (al-a'dam al-azaliyya). This prevents a misunderstanding about the statement that nothing besides God is eternal.
Eternal non-existences are not things; they are absences.
4
Understand the Azali vs. Qadim Distinction
Examine the discussion on whether 'azali' and 'qadim' are synonymous. Note the view of Ibn al-Tilmisani that they are, and al-Sa'd's refinement that 'azali' is more general, applying even to non-existences, while 'qadim' is reserved for self-subsisting entities without beginning.
Allah is described by both terms, but the distinction matters for other existents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القدم القِدَمُ بِالذَّاتِ فاعلم أي : القدم الذاتي، بمعنى: أنَّه تعالى قديم لذاته لا لعلَّة قديمة اقتضت وجوده، تعالى عن ذلك. وليس المراد بالقدم الذاتي ما قابل القدم بالغير، كما يقول الفلسفي، لقيام البرهان القاطع على أنَّه لا شيء قديم بالغير، وأنَّ كلَّ ما سوى الله وصفاته حادث كما تقدم. ومعنى القدم : سلبُ الأَوَّليَّة ؛ أي: أنَّه تعالى لا أوَّلية لوجوده. اتصاف قوله : ( وأن كل ما سوى الله أي من الموجودات، فلا ينافي الأعدام الأزليَّة بالقدم. قوله : (ومعنى القدم : سلب الأوَّليَّة) : أي : ويقال أيضاً: هو عدم الأوَّليَّة، أو عدم افتتاح الوجود وهل الأزلي مرادف للقديم؟ وهو ما قاله ابن التلمساني وأئمَّة اللُّغة ، (۱) فهما ما لا أوَّل له عدميّاً كان أو وجودياً، قائماً بنفسه أو لا وقال السعد: الأزليُّ أعمُّ من القديم، إذ القديم ما قام بنفسه، ولا أوّل لوجوده، والأزلي ما لا أوَّل له عدميّاً أو وجوديّاً، قائماً بنفسه أو بالذات العليَّة ، والأعدام الأزليَّة كذلك، وأمَّا ذات الله فيقال لها : أزليَّة قديمة) (۲) .
Pre-eternality: Pre-eternality by essence (al-qidam bil-dhat) – know, i.e., essential pre-eternality, meaning that He, exalted, is eternal by His essence, not due to an eternal cause that necessitated His existence, exalted is He above that. And what is meant by essential pre-eternality is not the opposite of pre-eternality by another (qadim bil-ghayr), as the philosopher says, because of the decisive proof that there is nothing eternal by another, and that everything other than God and His attributes is originated (hadith) as previously mentioned. And the meaning of pre-eternality (al-qidam) is the negation of beginning (salb al-awwaliyya); i.e., He, exalted, has no beginning to His existence. The connection of His saying: (And that everything other than God, i.e., from among existents, does not contradict eternal non-existences with pre-eternality). His saying: (And the meaning of pre-eternality: negation of beginning): i.e., it is also said: it is the absence of beginning, or the absence of the initiation of existence. And is al-azali synonymous with al-qadim? That is what Ibn al-Tilmisani and the imams of language said: they are both that which has no beginning, whether non-existent or existent, subsisting by itself or not. And al-Sa'd said: al-azali is more general than al-qadim, for al-qadim is that which subsists by itself and has no beginning to its existence, while al-azali is that which has no beginning, whether non-existent or existent, subsisting by itself or by the Essence of the Most High; and eternal non-existences are likewise. As for the Essence of God, it is said of it: azali and qadim.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of pre-eternality (al-qidam) as applied to God. It begins by stating that God is eternal by His essence (qadim bil-dhat), not due to an external cause. It rejects the philosophical concept of 'qadim bil-ghayr' (eternal through another) because there is a decisive proof that nothing other than God is eternal. The meaning of qidam is the negation of a beginning (salb al-awwaliyya). The passage then clarifies that the expression 'everything other than God' in a previous quote includes only existents, not eternal non-existences. Finally, the author discusses the terms 'azali' and 'qadim'. According to Ibn al-Tilmisani and language scholars, they are synonymous: both refer to anything without a beginning, whether existent or non-existent, self-subsisting or not. However, al-Sa'd distinguishes them: qadim applies only to what subsists by itself and has no beginning, while azali is more general and can apply to non-existences as well. God's Essence is described by both terms.

Key Terms
القدم
القدم الذاتي
القدم بالغير
سلب الأولية
الأزلي
القديم
الأعدام الأزلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Existence without end.
B) Negation of beginning (salb al-awwaliyya).
C) Existence through another.
D) Both A and B.

Key Takeaway
The attribute of pre-eternality means Allah has no beginning, and this is essential to Him, not derived from another.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that Allah is qadim bil-dhat—eternal by His essence, not by any cause. You, by contrast, were created from nothing and depend on Him for every moment of your existence. Does your daily life reflect that desperate dependence, or do you act as if you are self-sufficient? What would change if you truly felt your absolute contingency every second?
?
Al-Sa'd teaches that eternal non-existences (like your non-existence before birth) are azali but not qadim. Your past sins no longer exist—they are non-existent now. Yet Allah's forgiveness is azali and qadim. How does knowing that His mercy has no beginning and no end affect your willingness to repent of a sin you have repeated many times? Will you turn to Him now?
?
The author rejects the idea that anything besides Allah can be eternal through another. Are there people, objects, or ideas in your life that you treat as if they will always be there—that you cannot imagine living without? Consciously name one such attachment. How does the doctrine of al-qidam challenge you to hold it less tightly and to put your ultimate trust in Allah alone?

Definition of Qidam and the Distinction between Azali and Qadim
Al-Sawi defines qidam and discusses the relationship between azali and qadim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise meaning of qidam as a divine attribute and how azali and qadim differ in scope.

Core Idea
Qidam is the negation of beginning, but qadim specifically applies to self-subsistent beings like Allah.

This passage from Al-Sawi's Hashiyah lays the groundwork for understanding Allah's eternal nature. He defines qidam (eternality) as a necessary attribute and clarifies an important terminological distinction between 'azali' and 'qadim' that is often misunderstood. Let's examine the text to grasp these foundational concepts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Al-Sawi first defines qidam as essential and then explains its meaning as negation of priority.
2
Identify the definition of qidam
Locate the definition: 'ومعنى القدم : سلب الأَوَّليَّة' (the meaning of qidam is negation of priority). Understand what 'negation of priority' means for Allah's existence.
3
Compare azali and qadim
Trace Al-Sawi's discussion of whether azali and qadim are synonymous. Note the two views: Ibn al-Tilimsani says they are, while al-Sa'd says azali is broader. Understand why this distinction matters.
This clarifies that qadim applies only to self-subsistent entities like Allah.

القِدَمُ بِالذَّاتِ فاعلم أي : القدم الذاتي، بمعنى: أنَّه تعالى قديم لذاته لا لعلَّة قديمة اقتضت وجوده، تعالى عن ذلك.

The qidam by essence – know that it is the essential qidam, meaning that He, exalted, is eternal by His essence, not due to an eternal cause that necessitated His existence, exalted is He above that. And what is meant by essential qidam is not that which is opposed to qidam by another, as the philosopher says, because of the conclusive proof that nothing is eternal by another, and that everything other than Allah and His attributes is originated as has preceded. And the meaning of qidam is the negation of priority; that is, that He, exalted, has no priority for His existence. His saying: 'And that everything other than Allah, i.e., from existents, does not contradict the eternal non-existents with qidam.' His saying: 'And the meaning of qidam is negation of priority' – that is, it is also said: it is the absence of priority, or the absence of the beginning of existence. And is al-azali synonymous with al-qadim? That is what Ibn al-Tilimsani and the leading linguists said, (1) that both are that which has no beginning, whether non-existent or existent, self-subsistent or not. And al-Sa'd said: al-azali is more general than al-qadim, for al-qadim is that which subsists by itself and has no beginning for its existence, while al-azali is that which has no beginning, whether non-existent or existent, subsisting by itself or by the Supreme Essence, and the eternal non-existents are likewise. As for the Essence of Allah, it is called azali and qadim. (2) (1) Sharh al-Ma'alim (p. 412), and refer to Taj al-'Arus, entry (Azal). (2) Sharh al-Maqasid (1/130-71/20) Dar al-Ma'arif al-Nu'maniyyah edition. (130/1)
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of qidam (eternality/past eternity) for Allah and clarifies the distinction between the terms azali and qadim. It begins by specifying that qidam here is essential qidam, meaning Allah is eternal by His own essence, not because of an eternal cause. This refutes the philosophical notion of an eternal cause. Then it explains that essential qidam is not counterpart to qidam by another, because everything other than Allah is originated. Then the meaning of qidam is given as 'negation of priority,' i.e., no beginning to His existence. Then it discusses the phrase about eternal non-existents not contradicting qidam. Then it quotes the text: 'The meaning of qidam is negation of priority,' and explains that it is also absence of beginning. It then asks if azali is synonymous with qadim, and presents the view of Ibn al-Tilimsani and linguists that both refer to that which has no beginning, whether abstract or concrete, self-subsistent or not. Then al-Sa'd al-Taftazani is cited: azali is more general than qadim; qadim applies to that which subsists by itself (i.e., Allah), while azali applies to anything without beginning, including non-existents. So Allah's essence is both azali and qadim, but qadim is specific to self-subsistent beings.

Misconception: That 'azali' and 'qadim' are exactly synonymous and interchangeable for all beings.
Correction: While some scholars consider them synonymous, al-Sa'd clarifies that 'qadim' is restricted to self-subsistent entities like Allah, whereas 'azali' can also describe beginningless non-existents.

Key Takeaway
Qidam is the negation of beginning, and while all qadim are azali, not all azali are qadim; qadim is specific to self-subsistent entities like Allah.

?
The passage teaches that even non-existents (like the state before creation) are described as azali, but only Allah is qadim. Are there any 'non-existents' in your life—dreams, regrets, or imagined scenarios—that you treat as if they are eternal and self-subsistent? What would it mean to release your grip on that illusion and anchor your hope only in the Self-Subsistent, Qadim Lord? Write a short prayer asking Allah to purify your heart from false permanence.

Do you sometimes attribute a sense of self-subsistence to created things—your health, wealth, relationships—as if they could stand on their own without Allah? Identify one such thing and list three ways its existence depends entirely on Allah moment by moment. How will this knowledge change your attitude toward that blessing today?

Allah's Qidam: Proof and Refutation of Circularity and Infinite Regress
Al-Sawi presents the proof for Allah's eternality and refutes circularity and infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof for Allah's eternality and why both circularity and infinite regress are impossible in the chain of originators.

Core Idea
If Allah were not eternal, the chain of causes would end in absurdity.

Sanusi begins with a straightforward proof: if Allah were not eternal, He would be originated, requiring an originator. That originator, being similar, would also need an originator, leading either to circularity or infinite regress. Both are logically impossible, thus Allah must be eternal. This lesson walks through the argument and its refutations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the main proof
The argument assumes that if something is not eternal, it must have been brought into existence, requiring a cause. This cause, if similar in nature, would also require a cause, leading to a chain.
This is the classic kalam cosmological argument.
2
Identify the two impossible outcomes
The chain can either loop back (circularity) or continue forever (infinite regress). Both are deemed impossible.
3
Learn why circularity is invalid
Circularity requires each to be prior and posterior to the other, and even to itself, which is contradictory.
Impossibility of circularity is considered obvious.
4
Learn why infinite regress is invalid
Infinite regress leads to an infinite number of dependent, originated gods, contradicting the nature of divinity.
This refutation relies on the attributes of God.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Since both outcomes are impossible, the assumption that Allah is not eternal is false; therefore, Allah is eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل اتصافه تعالى بالقدم
إذ لو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثاً، تعالى عن ذلك، فيلزم افتقاره إلى محدث، لما مرّ، ثم محدثه كذلك، لانعقاد التماثل بينهما، وذلك مُفْضِ إلى الدور أو التّسلسل ؛ لأنَّ المماثل الثاني مَثَلاً إن كان المحدث له هو الأول فالدَّور، وإن استمرَّ العدد إلى غير نهاية فالتسلسل، وكلاهما محال .
بطلان الدور:
أمَّا استحالة الدَّور : فظاهرة؛ لأنَّه يلزم عليه تقدم كلِّ منهما على صاحبه وتأخره عنه، وهو جمع بين متنافيين بل ويلزم عليه أيضاً تقدم كلِّ واحد منهما على نفسه وتأخُرُه عنها، وهو جلى البطلان .
بطلان التسلسل
وأمَّا التّسلسل : فلأنَّه يؤدّي إلى وجود آلهة لا نهاية لها، كلٌّ منها متّصف بالحدوث والعجز والافتقار، وهو باطل قطعاً؛ لأنَّه مُنافٍ لمقام الألوهية من القدرة والغنى المطلق، إذ العاجز الفقير لا يصح أن يكون خالقاً للعالم البديع الإتقان.
قوله : (إذ لو لم يكن قديماً ... إلخ ) : شروع في تقرير الدليل التفصيلي
القديم
قوله: (فظاهرة) أي واضحة سهلة ،الأخذ، وليس المراد بديهية وإلا فلا يحتاج للدليل عليها مع أنه أقامه بقوله؛ لأنه يلزم عليه ... إلخ.
قوله: (وأما التسلسل ) : أي : بيان استحالته.
Proof of His, exalted, being characterized by qidam: If He were not eternal, He would be originated, exalted is He above that, and would then necessitate dependence on an originator, as has passed, then that originator would be likewise, because of the establishment of similarity between them, and that leads to circularity or infinite regress; because the second similar, for example, if its originator is the first, then there is circularity, and if the number continues to infinity, then there is infinite regress, and both are impossible. Invalidity of circularity: As for the impossibility of circularity: it is obvious; because it necessitates each of them being prior to the other and posterior to it, which is a combination of two contradictories. Rather, it also necessitates each of them being prior to itself and posterior to itself, and that is clearly false. Invalidity of infinite regress: As for infinite regress: because it leads to the existence of infinite gods, each characterized by origination, incapacity, and dependence, and that is absolutely false; because it contradicts the station of divinity with respect to power and absolute self-sufficiency, since the incapable and dependent cannot be the creator of the world of perfect craftsmanship. His saying: 'If He were not eternal... etc.' : a beginning in stating the detailed proof. Al-qadim. His saying: 'So it is obvious' – meaning clear and easy to grasp, and what is meant is not self-evident, otherwise he would not need proof for it, while he established it by his saying: 'because it necessitates... etc.' His saying: 'And as for infinite regress' – that is, an explanation of its impossibility.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents the proof for Allah's attribute of qidam (eternality). The argument begins by positing that if Allah were not eternal, He would be originated (hadith). An originated being requires an originator (muhdith). That originator, being similar in being originated, would also need an originator, and so on. This leads to either circularity (dawr) or an infinite regress (tasalsul). Both are impossible. The passage then elaborates on the impossibility of circularity: it would require each to be prior and posterior to the other, and even prior and posterior to itself, which is contradictory. The impossibility of infinite regress is shown: it leads to an infinite number of gods, each characterized by origination, incapacity (ajz), and need (iftiqar), which contradicts the nature of divinity that demands absolute power and self-sufficiency. An incapable and dependent being cannot be the creator of the highly precise world. The commentary then clarifies that the first statement is the start of the detailed proof, that 'obvious' means clear, not self-evident, and the third commentary simply notes that the section on infinite regress explains its impossibility.

Key Terms
قدم (qidam)
حدوث (huduth)
محدث (muhdith)
تماثل (tamathul)
دور (dawr)
تسلسل (tasalsul)
محال (muhal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An infinite chain of causes is logically possible.
Correction: The text demonstrates that an infinite regress of originators leads to an infinite number of dependent, incapable gods, which contradicts the necessary attributes of divinity (power and self-sufficiency).

Checkpoint
According to the proof, what would happen if there were an infinite regress of originators?
A) It would prove the existence of many gods.
B) It would lead to circularity.
C) It would result in an infinite number of gods, each being originated and dependent, which is impossible for divinity.
D) It would be possible because the chain could continue endlessly.

Key Takeaway
Allah must be eternal because any alternative leads to logically impossible chains of causes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a blessing you received today. Did you trace it back to its ultimate source, or did you stop at the immediate cause? How does acknowledging Allah’s qidam change your gratitude?
?
If you truly believe that circularity and infinite regress are impossible, then every chain of dependence must end in Allah. Does your daily reliance reflect this conclusion, or do you still act as if created things are self-sufficient?
?
The passage argues that an infinite series of dependent beings would clash with the absolute power and perfection of divinity. When you look at your own weaknesses and needs, do you humbly accept your complete dependence on the Eternal, or do you unconsciously try to build self-sufficiency apart from Him?

Definition and Proof of Divine Everlastingness (Baqa)
Sanusi defines baqa and proves it from pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that baqa is a negative attribute defined as the negation of finality, and its proof based on the pre-eternity of Allah.

Core Idea
Everlastingness is not a quality but the absence of an end.

In this passage, Sanusi introduces the second negative attribute: everlastingness (baqa). He first defines it as the negation of finality, then provides a concise rational proof: if something is pre-eternal, its non-existence is impossible. This establishes that God has no end. The commentary clarifies alternative phrasings and the structure of the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of baqa
Read the opening line where Sanusi defines baqa as 'salb al-ākhiyya'. Notice that he emphasizes it is a negative attribute.
2
Understand the proof from pre-eternity
Follow the proof: because pre-eternity is established, non-existence is impossible. Reason through the hypothetical: if non-existence were possible, it would need a specifying factor, making it originated, contradicting pre-eternity.
3
Review the alternative definitions
The commentary offers two alternative definitions: 'absence of finality' and 'absence of termination of existence'. Reflect on how they all convey the same idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البقاء
(و) ثاني الصفات السَّلبيَّة ( البَقَا) بالقصر للضرورة، وهو سلب الآخرية :أي: نفيها ؛ أي أنَّه تعالى لا آخر لوجوده تعالى.
دليل اتصافه تعالى بالبقاء :

Everlastingness: And the second of the negative attributes is everlastingness (al-baqā) shortened for metrical necessity, which is the negation of finality: i.e., its denial; meaning that He, exalted, has no end to His existence. Proof of His being described by everlastingness: Because that whose pre-eternity is established, its non-existence is impossible; otherwise non-existence would be possible for it, so it would need a specifying factor, thus becoming originated, not pre-eternal, when its pre-eternity has been established. His saying: (And it is the negation of finality) means: and it is also said: it is the absence of finality, or the absence of termination of existence. His saying: (Because that whose pre-eternity is established... etc.) is a beginning of detailed presentation of the proof for everlastingness.

Commentary
This passage defines and proves the attribute of everlastingness (baqa). The author states that baqa is the second negative attribute (after pre-eternity) and is defined as the negation of finality—i.e., God has no end to His existence. The proof is given: if something is pre-eternal, its non-existence is impossible. If non-existence were possible, it would need a factor to bring it about, making it originated, contradicting its established pre-eternity. The commentary clarifies that baqa can also be defined as the absence of finality or termination of existence, and notes that the proof begins from the premise of pre-eternity.

Baqa is a negative attribute meaning God has no end, proven by the impossibility of non-existence for what is pre-eternal.

Proof of Allah's Eternity via Reductio ad Absurdum
Al-Sawi presents a reductio proof for Allah's eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic theologians use reductio ad absurdum to prove that Allah is eternal (qadim) by showing that denying it leads to impossible consequences.

Core Idea
What leads to an impossibility is itself impossible, so eternity of Allah is proven.

In this lesson, we encounter a classic kalam proof for Allah's eternity. The argument uses a reductio approach: if we assume Allah is not eternal, that leads to absurdities like circularity or infinite regress. Since those are impossible, the assumption must be false, establishing that Allah is eternal. Al-Sawi presents this proof concisely, with commentary clarifying key terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the original Arabic passage and its English translation to get the flow of the proof.
Notice the concise style of kalam arguments.
2
Identify key terms
Understand terms like afḍā (leads to), muḥāl (impossible), lawāzim (necessary concomitants), malzūmāt (things characterized), and how they fit the argument.
These terms recur in many kalam proofs.
3
Understand the reductio structure
Recognize that the argument assumes the opposite (non-eternity) and derives an impossibility (circularity or infinite regress), thereby proving the opposite false.
This is a classical logical technique.
4
Connect to broader methodology
See that this proof exemplifies the principle: if a premise leads to impossible consequences, the premise itself is impossible.
This is a foundational rule in kalam reasoning.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Confirm that the proof successfully establishes qidam (eternity) of Allah, which is the desired conclusion.
The phrase 'fa thabata al-qidam' signals the proof is complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما أفضى إلى المحال - وهو عدم القدم – محال، إذ استحالة اللوازم تقتضي استحالة الملزومات فثبت القدم، وهو المطلوب. قوله : (وما أفضى إلى المحال) : أي : أدي إليه. قوله : (إذ استحالة اللوازم) : أي : وهي الدور أو التّسلسل . وقوله : (تقتضي استحالة الملزومات) أي: وهو الأوَّليَّة
And what leads to the impossible - which is non-eternity - is impossible, because the impossibility of the necessary concomitants necessitates the impossibility of the things characterized by them, so eternity is established, and that is the desired. His statement: 'And what leads to the impossible' means: leads to it. His statement: 'Because the impossibility of the necessary concomitants' means: they are circularity or infinite regress. And His statement: 'necessitates the impossibility of the things characterized by them' means: which is priority.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the eternity (qidam) of Allah. It begins with a conditional: 'what leads to the impossible is impossible.' The impossible here is non-eternity (ʿadam al-qidam). The argument states that if non-eternity were possible, it would lead to an impossibility—namely circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul). Since the impossibility of the necessary concomitants implies the impossibility of the premise, non-eternity is impossible, so eternity is established. The commentary clarifies the key terms: 'what leads to' (afḍā) means leads to; the impossible here refers to non-eternity; the 'necessary concomitants' (al-lawāzim) are circularity or infinite regress; and the 'things characterized by them' (al-malzūmāt) is priority (al-awwaliyya), meaning that which is prior. The argument follows the kalam method of reductio: if a premise entails an absurdity, the premise must be false.

Key Terms

محال
عدم القدم
استحالة اللوازم
الملزومات
الدور
التسلسل
الأوَّليَّة
القدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is circular reasoning.
Correction: It is a valid reductio ad absurdum: it shows that denying Allah's eternity leads to an absurdity, so the denial is false.

Checkpoint
What does the argument in this lesson prove about Allah?
A) That He is eternal (qadim)
B) That He is everlasting (baqi)
C) That He is self-subsistent (qaim bi-nafsih)
D) That He is one (wahid)

Key Takeaway
The eternity of Allah is proven because denying it leads to impossibilities like circularity or infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If denying Allah's eternity leads to absurdities like circularity or infinite regress, where in your own thinking might you be holding onto a belief that leads to logical or spiritual contradiction? Are you willing to let it go to embrace divine truth?
?
The proof shows that non-eternity is impossible for Allah. Does your daily trust in Allah reflect this conviction, or do you sometimes act as if His care is limited by time? What would change if you fully lived as if He is eternal and ever-present?
?
This argument uses reductio: what leads to impossibility is itself impossible. What area of your life—a habit, a thought pattern, a relationship—is leading you to spiritual impossibility? Can you apply this same reasoning to reject that path and return to what is necessary for your soul?

Defining Baqa' and Its Proof from Qidam
Al-Sawi defines baqa' and gives its proof from qidam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how baqa' is defined as a negative attribute and why it necessarily follows from qidam.

Core Idea
Baqa' is not a positive attribute; it simply denies an end to Allah's existence.

Al-Sawi begins by defining baqa' (everlastingness) as the negation of an end. He then provides a rational proof: if something is eternal (qadim), its non-existence is impossible. This passage establishes the second negative attribute and its logical basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own words convey the definition and proof.
Notice the concise style of the definition.
2
Identify the definition of baqa'
Find where Al-Sawi defines baqa' as 'salb al-akiriyya' (negation of otherness). Understand that it is a negative attribute.
Baqa' is not a positive quality; it only denies an end.
3
Understand the proof from qidam
The proof states: whatever is established as qadim cannot admit non-existence, because if non-existence were possible, it would need a cause and would be originated, contradicting its eternity.
This is a logical necessity linking qidam and baqa'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البقاء (و) ثاني الصفات السَّلبيَّة ( البَقَا) بالقصر للضرورة، وهو سلب الآخرية :أي: نفيها ؛ أي أنَّه تعالى لا آخر لوجوده تعالى. دليل اتصافه تعالى بالبقاء : لأنَّ ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه، وإلا لجاز عليه العدم، فيحتاج إلى مرجّح فيكون حادثاً لا قديماً، كيف وقد ثبت قدمه . قوله : (وهو سلب (الآخريَّة) : أي : ويقال أيضاً : هو عدم الآخريَّة، أو عدم اختتام الوجود. إن قلت : إنَّ وجوب الوجود يغني عن القدم والبقاء والمخالفة للحوادث . أجيب بأنَّه لمَّا كان التَّوحيد أهم الأمور المطلوبة من الشخص، إذ به ينجو من دار البوار ; وضَّح علماء الكلام المقام، ولم يكتفوا بدلالة الالتزام. قوله : ( لأنَّ ما ثبت قدمه ... إلخ) : شروع في تقرير الدليل على البقاء
Al-Baqa' (and) the second of the negative attributes (al-baqa') shortened out of necessity, and it is the negation of otherness: i.e., its denial; meaning that He, exalted, has no end to His existence. The proof that He, exalted, is characterized by baqa': because that whose qidam is established, its non-existence is impossible; otherwise non-existence would be possible for it, so it would need a preponderator and would be originated, not eternal, how can it be when its qidam has been established. His statement: 'and it is the negation of otherness' means: it is also said: it is the absence of otherness, or the absence of termination of existence. If you say: Verily wajib al-wujud suffices for qidam, baqa', and dissimilarity to originated things. The answer: Because tawhid is the most important of what is required from the person, for by it he escapes the abode of perdition; the scholars of kalam clarified the matter, and they were not content with the implication of entailment. His statement: 'Because that whose qidam is established... etc.' is the beginning of presenting the proof of baqa'.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage defines and proves the attribute of baqa' (everlastingness) as the second negative attribute. It is defined as the negation of having an end (salb al-akiriyya), meaning Allah's existence has no termination. The proof argues that whatever is proven eternal (qadim) cannot admit non-existence, because if non-existence were possible, it would need a preponderator to bring it about, which would make it originated (hadith), contradicting its eternity. Thus, baqa' follows necessarily from qidam. The commentary notes an objection: that wajib al-wujud (necessary existence) already suffices and dispenses with proving qidam, baqa', and mukhalafa lil-hawadith. The answer is that because tawhid is the most crucial requirement for salvation, kalam scholars detailed these attributes explicitly, rather than relying on entailment (dalalat al-iltizam). This shows pedagogical care: they made the argument clear for all students.

Key Terms
البقاء
الآخريَّة
القدم
العدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqa' is a positive attribute like power or will.
Correction: Baqa' is a negative attribute; it merely denies an end, not add a quality.

Checkpoint
Why does the proof for baqa' rely on qidam?
A) Because qidam and baqa' are synonyms
B) Because if something is eternal, its non-existence is impossible
C) Because baqa' is a necessary concomitant of wajib al-wujud
D) Because qidam is the only proof for baqa'

Key Takeaway
Baqa' is the necessary attribute that Allah's existence has no end, proven by His eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah’s existence has no end, then your life in this world is just a fleeting moment in the face of an eternal reality. How does that perspective change what you prioritize today—this hour?
?
This lesson shows that baqa' is a negative attribute: it only tells us what Allah is not (not having an end). Are you content with knowing Allah through what He is not, or do you find it unsettling? What does your reaction reveal about your heart?
?
The proof for baqa' rests on the impossibility of Allah changing or ceasing to be. Does your daily life reflect a deep-seated belief in Allah's unchanging nature, or do you act as if He could be replaced by other concerns? Commit to one concrete change you will make today to reorient your life toward the Eternal.

The Objection and Answer: Why Kalam Scholars Explicitly Prove Divine Attributes
Al-Sawi answers an objection about sufficiency of wajib al-wujud for proving attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why kalam scholars did not rely solely on entailment (dalalat al-iltizam) but explicitly proved attributes like baqa'.

Core Idea
Tawhid is so crucial that scholars made every attribute explicit rather than leave it to implication.

Here, al-Sawi addresses an objection: if Allah is wajib al-wujud, doesn't that already imply His everlastingness? The answer reveals a pedagogical principle: because tawhid is the most important goal, scholars clarify rather than rely on implicit entailments. This lesson explains their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector argues that wajib al-wujud (necessary existence) alone suffices to imply qidam, baqa', and other negative attributes, making separate proofs redundant.
This is a valid logical point: necessary existence entails eternity and everlastingness.
2
See the answer: tawhid's importance
Al-Sawi answers that tawhid is the most crucial matter for salvation, so scholars explained each attribute explicitly rather than relying on implication.
The goal of kalam is practical: guiding people to tawhid.
3
Reflect on the method
Scholars rejected relying solely on dalalat al-iltizam (implication of entailment) because clarity and certainty are paramount for tawhid.
This shows the pedagogical care in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The proof that He, exalted, is characterized by baqa': because that whose qidam is established, its non-existence is impossible; otherwise non-existence would be possible for it, so it would need a preponderator and would be originated, not eternal, how can it be when its qidam has been established. His statement: 'Because that whose qidam is established... etc.' is the beginning of presenting the proof of baqa'.

It is defined as the negation of having an end (salb al-akiriyya), meaning Allah's existence has no termination. The proof argues that whatever is proven eternal (qadim) cannot admit non-existence, because if non-existence were possible, it would need a preponderator to bring it about, which would make it originated (hadith), contradicting its eternity. Self-Subsistence and the Divine 'Nafs'
Al-Sawi defines qiyamuhu binafsihi and defends using 'nafs' for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of Allah's self-subsistence (qiyamuhu binafsihi) and how it permits using the term 'nafs' for Him, with scriptural evidence.

Core Idea
Allah's self-subsistence means He depends on nothing; thus calling Him 'Self' is proper.

Al-Sawi turns to the third negative attribute, establishing that Allah is self‑subsistent. The proof connects this to qidam and baqaʼ. He then addresses a linguistic nuance about the preposition 'bi' and uses the attribute to justify applying the word 'nafs' (self) to Allah, citing the Quran and Sunnah. This defends against those who restrict such usage to figurative similarity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's structure become familiar before analysis.
The passage begins with the proof for self‑subsistence, then discusses the preposition 'bi', and ends with the evidence for 'nafs'.
2
Understand the two proofs for self‑subsistence
Notice that Al‑Sawi gives two ways to prove the attribute: either through qidam (eternity) or through wajib al‑baqa' (necessary permanence). Both show that non‑existence is impossible.
These proofs are condensed; try to see the logical link: if non‑existence were possible, eternity would be impossible.
3
Examine the interpretations of 'bi'
Al‑Sawi lists three possible meanings of the preposition in 'qiyamuhu binafsihi'. The closest is 'in' (fi), meaning Allah subsists in Himself, not by another.
This clarifies that 'bi' does not imply instrumentality or causality; it signifies inherent subsistence.
4
See how self‑subsistence permits using 'nafs' for Allah
From this attribute, the permissibility of calling Allah 'nafs' is derived. Al‑Sawi cites Quranic verses and a hadith as evidence, refuting the view that restricts such usage to stylistic similarity (mushakala).
The objection based on Q. 5:116 is addressed; the preponderant view is literal permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) ثالث الصفات السَّلبيَّة (قيامه) تعالى (بنفسه)، وهذا الدَّليل إمَّا القدم نفسه أو دليله ; لأنَّ لك أن تقول : لو جاز عليه طرقُ العدم ; لاستحال عليه القدم ; لأنَّ من جاز عدمه استحال قدمه، أو تقول: لو لم يتّصف بوجوب البقاء; لجاز عليه العدم، ولو جاز عليه العدم; لكان حادثاً ... إلى آخر ما قال الشَّرح . قوله: قيامه بنفسه) اختلف في معنى هذه الباء، فقيل : للآلة، وقيل: للسببية، وقيل: بمعنى (في) وهو الأقرب، والمعنى أنه مستغن في نفسه ليس باعتبار شيء آخر، ويؤخذ من هذه الصفة جواز إطلاق النفس على الله تعالى(۱)، وقد ورد ذلك قال تعالى: كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ : الرَّحْمَةُ (٢) ، (وَأَصْطَنَعْتُكَ لِنَفْسِي ) (۳). وقال عليه الصَّلاة والسَّلام : لا أحصي ثناء عليك، أنت كما أثنيت على نفسك» (٤) . .. إلى غير ذلك، خلافاً لمن يقول : إنَّه لا يجوز إطلاقها على الله إلا في مقام المشاكلة; مستدلاً بقوله تعالى : تَعْلَمُ مَا فِي نَفْسِي وَلَا أَعْلَمُ مَا فِي نَفْسِكَ (٥)
And the third of the negative attributes (His subsistence) exalted (by Himself). And this proof is either qidam itself or its proof; because you may say: if non-existence were possible for Him, then qidam would be impossible; because that whose non-existence is possible, its qidam is impossible. Or you may say: if He were not characterized by wajib al-baqa', then non-existence would be possible for Him, and if non-existence were possible for Him, He would be originated... to the end of what the Sharh said. His statement: 'His subsistence by Himself' – there is disagreement on the meaning of this 'bi'. It is said: for instrumentality, said: for causality, and said: with the meaning of 'in', and it is the closest. The meaning is that He is independent in His essence, not by virtue of anything else. And from this attribute is taken the permissibility of applying 'nafs' (self/soul) to Allah, exalted, and it has been reported: Allah said: 'Your Lord has written mercy on Himself' (Quran 6:54), and 'I have chosen you for Myself' (Quran 20:41). And the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'I cannot enumerate praise of You, You are as You have praised Yourself.' ... and so on, contrary to those who say that it is not permissible to apply it to Allah except in the context of similarity (mushakala), adducing His statement: 'You know what is in my self and I do not know what is in Your Self' (Quran 5:116).
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage presents the third negative attribute: qiyamuhu binafsihi (self-subsistence). It means Allah is independent, not needing any other to sustain Him. The proof for this attribute is tied to qidam or baqa': if non-existence were possible, qidam would be impossible; or if baqa' were not necessary, non-existence would be possible, implying huduth. The commentary then discusses the preposition 'bi'. Three interpretations are given: instrumental (bi means 'by means of'), causal (bi means 'because of'), and the closest is that it means 'in' (fi), indicating that Allah subsists in Himself, not by another. From this attribute, the permissibility of calling Allah 'nafs' (self) is derived, supported by Quranic verses and hadith. The phrase 'Your Lord has written mercy on Himself' uses 'nafs'. This refutes those who restrict such usage to stylistic similarity (mushakala) and claim it is not literal, citing the verse 'You know what is in my self and I do not know what is in Your Self'. Al-Sawi argues that the preponderant view is permissibility, as the texts show.

Key Terms
القيام بالنفس
القدم
وجوب البقاء
الباء
النفس
المشاكلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the attribute 'qiyamuhu binafsihi' implies Allah has a physical location or is corporeal.
Correction: It simply affirms His independence from anything else, not spatiality; self‑subsistence is a negative attribute negating need.

Checkpoint

A) Instrumentality (bi = by means of)
B) Causality (bi = because of)
C) It means 'in' (fi) signifying inherent subsistence
D) It means 'with' (ma'a)

Key Takeaway
Allah's self‑subsistence affirms His absolute independence and justifies referring to Him with the term 'nafs' as authentically revealed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Self-Subsistence: The Third Negative Attribute
Defines self-subsistence and gives its proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of Allah's attribute of self-subsistence and how it is derived from the proof of pre-eternity.

Core Idea
Allah's self-subsistence means He is absolutely independent, needing no support.

The third negative attribute of Allah is self-subsistence (qiyāmuhu bi-nafsihi). This lesson unpacks its definition, its connection to pre-eternity, and the nuanced meaning of the preposition 'bi' in this phrase. Understanding this attribute deepens our grasp of Allah's independence from all creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on self-subsistence
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting the definition and the proof given.
2
Understand the proof linking to pre-eternity
The passage explains that the proof for self-subsistence is the same as for pre-eternity. Follow the logical conditional statements.
If non-existence were possible, pre-eternity would be impossible.
3
Analyze the preposition 'bi'
The passage discusses three possible meanings of 'bi' in 'bi-nafsihi'. Focus on why 'in the sense of 'in'' is preferred.
The meaning is that He subsists in Himself, not through another.
4
Reflect on the attribute's significance
Consider how this attribute emphasizes Allah's independence and negates any need for a sustaining cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القيام بالنفس
(و) ثالث الصفات السَّلبيَّة (قيامه) تعالى (بنفسه)،
وهذا الدَّليل إمَّا القدم نفسه أو دليله ؛ لأنَّ لك أن تقول : لو جاز عليه طرقُ العدم ؛ لاستحال عليه القدم ؛ لأنَّ من جاز عدمه استحال قدمه، أو تقول: لو لم يتّصف بوجوب البقاء ؛ لجاز عليه العدم، ولو جاز عليه العدم؛ لكان حادثاً ... إلى آخر ما قال الشَّرح .
قوله: قيامه بنفسه) اختلف في معنى هذه الباء، فقيل : للآلة، وقيل: للسببية، وقيل: بمعنى (في) وهو الأقرب، والمعنى أنه مستغن في نفسه ليس باعتبار شيء آخر، ويؤخذ من هذه الصفة جواز إطلاق النفس على الله تعالى(۱)، وقد ورد ذلك قال تعالى: كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ : الرَّحْمَةُ (٢) ، (وَأَصْطَنَعْتُكَ لِنَفْسِي ) (۳).
وقال عليه الصَّلاة والسَّلام : لا أحصي ثناء عليك، أنت كما أثنيت على نفسك» (٤) . .. إلى غير ذلك، خلافاً لمن يقول : إنَّه لا يجوز إطلاقها على الله إلا في مقام المشاكلة؛ مستدلاً بقوله تعالى : تَعْلَمُ مَا فِي نَفْسِي وَلَا
أَعْلَمُ مَا فِي نَفْسِكَ (٥)
Self-subsistence. And the third of the negative attributes is His (Exalted) self-subsistence. This proof is either [the proof for] pre-eternity itself or its evidence; for you may say: if non-existence were possible for Him, then pre-eternity would be impossible for Him, because whoever is possible to cease to exist, pre-eternity is impossible for him. Or you say: if He were not described with necessary perpetuity, then non-existence would be possible for Him, and if non-existence were possible for Him, He would be originated... up to the end of what the commentary said. His statement: 'His self-subsistence': there is disagreement about the meaning of this preposition 'bi'. It is said: for instrumentality, and it is said: for causality, and it is said: in the sense of 'in' (which is closest). And the meaning is that He is independent in Himself, not by consideration of another thing. And from this attribute is derived the permissibility of applying the word 'nafs' (self/soul) to Allah the Exalted, and this has come in the Qur'an: 'Your Lord has prescribed mercy upon Himself' (6:54) and 'And I have chosen you for Myself' (20:41). And the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'I cannot enumerate praise of You, You are as You have praised Yourself.' ... and other [texts], contrary to those who say that it is not permissible to apply it to Allah except in the context of rhetorical similitude, using as evidence His statement: 'You know what is in my soul and I do not know what is in Your soul' (5:116).
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage defines the third negative attribute of Allah: self-subsistence (qiyāmuhu bi-nafsihi). It first clarifies that the proof for this attribute is essentially the same as the proof for pre-eternity. Then it explains the different interpretations of the preposition 'bi' in the phrase, favoring the meaning 'in' (i.e., He subsists in Himself). The core meaning is that Allah is completely independent, not relying on anything else. The passage then addresses a related theological question: whether the word 'nafs' (soul/self) can be attributed to Allah. The author affirms that it is permissible, citing Quranic verses and a hadith, and refutes the opposing view that restricts its use to rhetorical similitude (mushākala) based on the verse 'You know what is in my soul and I do not know what is in Your soul.'

Key Terms
القيام بالنفس
الصفات السلبية
القدم
الباء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'self-subsistence' means Allah has a physical self or is composed.
Correction: It means absolute independence from any dependence or support, not a physical self.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which interpretation of the preposition 'bi' in 'qiyāmuhu bi-nafsihi' is considered closest?
A) For instrumentality
B) For causality
C) In the sense of 'in'
D) For accompaniment

Key Takeaway
Allah's self-subsistence means He is absolutely independent, relying on no cause or support, and this attribute is derived from His pre-eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What 'causes' in your life do you instinctively depend on as if they are independent, and how does remembering that Allah alone is self-subsistent challenge that dependence?
?
The proof ties self-subsistence to pre-eternity—Allah’s existence has no beginning. How does this reality confront your attachment to things that will inevitably end?
?
If you caught yourself thinking that Allah 'needs' your worship to sustain His sovereignty, what would that reveal about your understanding of His absolute independence, and how can you correct it?

Applying the Word 'Nafs' to Allah
Discusses permissibility of applying 'nafs' to Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the permissibility of attributing the word 'nafs' to Allah and the evidence used by both sides.

Core Idea
The word 'nafs' can be attributed to Allah based on Quran and Hadith, not restricted to rhetorical similitude.

The attribute of self-subsistence allows for the application of the word 'nafs' (self/soul) to Allah. However, some scholars restrict this to rhetorical contexts. This lesson examines the evidence from the Quran and Hadith and evaluates the opposing view based on the verse 'You know what is in my soul...'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on 'nafs'
Read from 'ويؤخذ من هذه الصفة...' to the end. Note the Quranic verses and hadith cited.
2
Identify the two positions
The author affirms permissibility; others allow only in rhetorical similitude (mushākala). Understand why.
3
Evaluate the opposing evidence
The opposing view uses verse 5:116. Consider how the author might respond.
4
Reflect on the implications
Why does this matter? It shows that attributes derived from Quranic language are valid without literal anthropomorphism.
